<span id="freeTextContainer3144240505853163002">Ladies and gentlemen, I ask your forgiveness for succumbing to the phenomenon known to historians as the "delights of Cumas", which prevent the great purposes from being carried out. I pledged to try to write a review of the books, which I read this summer, but molicie, and personal ambitions (you know it's much more comfortable to attack, and conquer, as Alexander the Great, Ecaster, or Bayan* of the 100 eyes well known, to preserve and conserve and manage the conquests. In this case it would b</span>
  <span id="freeText3144240505853163002" style="display:none">Ladies and gentlemen, I ask your forgiveness for succumbing to the phenomenon known to historians as the "delights of Cumas", which prevent the great purposes from being carried out. I pledged to try to write a review of the books, which I read this summer, but molicie, and personal ambitions (you know it's much more comfortable to attack, and conquer, as Alexander the Great, Ecaster, or Bayan* of the 100 eyes well known, to preserve and conserve and manage the conquests. In this case it would be more practical to reflect on my readings).<br />About Dragonwyck you have to say one thing, which is a book that was in the middle began to be read in Valladolid, and ended in Mojados. The one that was my first country reading. There are many things, which I do not remember from this book, but if I have an idea, and I was a bit of a cyclist with this book. I gave him a (3), but the real note, which corresponds to Anya Seton's novel would be a (3'5-3'75), perhaps, so he didn't rule it out to raise four stars. Because this novel, which served to make an interesting film adaptation, which unfortunately could not be seen directed by Joseph L. Mankiewicz, and performed by one of the most beautiful actresses in Hollywood Gene Tierney (the unforgettable"Laura" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/601799.Laura?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6...</a> ) , and perhaps by one of the best horror film actors Vincent Price <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film113648.html">https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film1...</a>. Because that's what this wonderful novel is a gothic story, which drinks a lot from other novels. The reason I didn't put four stars on it is because he considered, that his predecessors are a little better "Jane Eyre" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10210.Jane_Eyre?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> "The Secret Garden" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2998.The_Secret_Garden?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2...</a> and "Rebekah" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17899948-rebecca?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17899948-rebecca?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> In my opinion "Dragonwyck" owes a lot of the first, and the third. Her heroine Miranda (a precious name) is not a woman tanned by suffering, and despite the Calvinist father (in fact the father's faith is too axfisiante, and unattractive, in fact for me a flaw) does not have the religious concerns of Jane Eyre, who has matured , because her past cured her. Nor is she the naive, but innocent second wife of the charismatic, mysterious and ambiguous Mr. Max de Winter. This heroin seems more like a very immature naif to me. The one who reminds me the most is the unforgettable protagonist of Jane Austen's "Northanger Abbey" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/50398.Northanger_Abbey">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5...</a> Miranda may not dream of being the protagonist of a Gothic novel, as Morstand the unforgettable protagonist of "The Abbey of Northanger", but in living among cotton, and getting rid of the domestic country chores. I admit, one of the flaws I found in this novel is that it didn't empathize with the great characters. Miranda seemed to me a silly girl, and at times as selfish, as the protagonist of Bela Dona (an erotic film starring Nasthasa Hendridge, that of Species, very bad, that they put on antenna 3 that I do not recommend to see). The bad thing about the movie Bela Dona it's not the erotic scenes, but the selfishness of the protagonist. It is the story of a German couple in Hitler's time, who on business goes to Brazil, and there he is with a Brazilian. The immoral thing is that having Jewish friends the protagonist, who is not addicted to Hitler, but does not do with them, because she prefers to continue with illicit adultery. The same thing happens to Miranda is in love with Nicholas van Ryn, although more than in love I would say that she is fascinated by him, bewitched by him. This prevents her from becoming aware until almost the end of what her husband is doing to his tenants whom he treats as if they were servants of the gleba, despite the American revolution Van Ryn descendant of the Dutch still lives as a landowner. Nicholas van Ryn, he's a character that fascinates us, but we can't like it. I'm not a big fan of him because of his Hispanophobia, but it fits Van Ryn in good condition with a phrase that Geoffrey Parker <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/86948.Geoffrey_Parker">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> said of our fascinating King Philip II , "That you didn't know whether to love him or hate him." We know, that he is the villain, and that he only has one goal, that I will not say to uncover the plot of the novel, and for that he will stop at nothing. Nicholas Van Ryn is a book psychopath. I don't know if the Goodreads user, who comes close to this review. You've had the opportunity to watch the wonderful Crystal Jungle III film a revenge when John McLane/Bruce Willis gets to talk on the phone with Simon Gruber/Jeremy Irons and the psychiatrist detects all the psychopath's symptoms. It is one of the most memorable scenes in the history of cinema. The same thing is masterfully done by Anya Seton in this novel. I don't know if by inbreeding, by a curse (brilliant resource of the novelist), but Anya Seton describes in Nicholas Seton a psychopath of manual. Someone whose only problem is not only his reactionary opinions, but as the reader will see, who stops at nothing, to achieve his ends. . I know, it's propaganda to someone very dear, but it's very interesting to find the toxicological knowledge, which Anya Seton demonstrates, so I recommend this book (although the American edition is already sold out. A pity) <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12975242-los-venenos-en-la-literatura-policiaca?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> fascinating Lo9 of this novel is that the reader expects an evil character who is outrageous, but eye- Here comes the surprise Nicholas van Ryn, I do not know if out of satanic pride, or because he does feel some interest in Miranda is able to do good deeds. He's not as nice as Fosco*, but Nicholas van Ryn reminded me a lot of the psychopath in a Dutch film from which he made an American remake <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Vanishing_(film_1993)">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Van...</a> (the original movie, which is better, than the American one, weighs tragic in the end it was called Spoorloos <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film627268.html">https://www.filmaffinity.com/es/film6...</a> ) with Sandra Bullock, Jeff Bridges, and Kiefer Sutherland (eye the psycho path was not Keiefer Sutherland). This film the version I saw in the wonderful program of Tears in the Rain directed years ago by my favorite writer Juan Manuel de Prada <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/244771.Juan_Manuel_de_Prada">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> and the interesting José Carlos Somoza to which at last I read a novel (I didn't like it, but I think, it has great writer's <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/40535.Jos_Carlos_Somoza">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> ) <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://elespejoquerefleja.blogspot.com/2012/08/lagrimas-en-la-lluvia-los-videos.html">elespejoquerefleja.blogspot.com/2012/...</a>. But as much as this character is the soul, and the heart of the novel. It's impossible justify his actions, or love him, though he will leave us an important echo. The doctor, who completes the love triangle. We can empathize with his cause, but not with the methods, which he employs. Perhaps the only character I liked is the Irish maid, which is the only contact there is with Catholicism. It's a novel, which starts a little slow, but gets better, until it shows the great novel, which it actually is. It is a perfect X-ray of the nineteenth century, especially the time of Martin Van Buren, and the 40s of the nineteenth century. There are cameos of great writers of the time such as Fenimore Cooper (who remains as a person very attached to the old regime, a conservative), Herman Melville, but perhaps the most endearing moment is the encounter with Edgar Allan Por, where Nicholas van Ryn will show despite the i morbid his closest side to Jekyll. <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9121.James_Fenimore_Cooper">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1624.Herman_Melville">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4624490.Edgar_Allan_Poe">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> There is also a Gavroche moment*. The protagonist's disincrush with Nicholas Van Ryn is very well written. It's curious G.K. Chesterton <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/7014283.G_K_Chesterton">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> in his book of "Victorian Literature" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1011950.The_Victorian_Age_in_Literature?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> right said of the Bronte that one of its facets was to show men, including the lovable Rochester, as if they were monsters. This is exacerbated by Nicholas van Ryn, who is a dark, murderous version of Mr. Rochester. It is the embodiment of Emerson's individualistic theories, even in his atheism. Anya Seton demonstrates a great knowledge of human nature, but knows how to give a grand ending to her antagonist, and she brilliantly ends this novel. I have no choice but to congratulate the Spanish publisher Paper Books for this magnificent edition, and hopefully they will be encouraged to edit Anya Seton's "Avalón" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/36252.Avalon?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3...</a> Reading highly recommended, and I hope that Goodreads users like it more than I do.<br />*Both fictional characters of the Canadian novelist Thomas B. Costain, and appearing in "The Silver Chalice" and "The Black Rose" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5772434.Thomas_B_Costain">https://www.goodreads.com/author/show...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/122771.The_Silver_Chalice?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1...</a> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/401921.The_Black_Rose">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4...</a> <br />*Villain of Wilkie Collins' "The Lady in White" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5890.The_Woman_in_White?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5...</a> * Character of "The miserable" <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24280.Les_Mis_rables?ac=1&amp;from_search=true">https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2...</a># <br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2661925254" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2661925254" />
    <a title="Ann (Inky)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3299710-ann-inky"><img alt="Ann (Inky)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578635369p2/3299710.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2661925254?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ann (Inky)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ann (Inky)" href="/user/show/3299710-ann-inky">Ann (Inky)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781444788228" href="/book/show/23825775-dragonwyck">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299710-ann-inky?shelf=favorites-of-all-time">favorites-of-all-time</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299710-ann-inky?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299710-ann-inky?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299710-ann-inky?shelf=love-tales">love-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299710-ann-inky?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299710-ann-inky?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299710-ann-inky?shelf=on-my-shelf">on-my-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3299710-ann-inky?shelf=books-ive-reviewed">books-ive-reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2661925254" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15007323751722102256"><blockquote>
  <i>"What a horrible thing for her to say—she was crazy then, poor thing?"<br/>"Crazy with fear and misery, p’tite. <b>A tropic flower cannot live without sun. A soul cannot live without love.'"</b></i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Miranda, <i>Dragonwyck</i>'s heroine, is a character very near and dear to my heart; mostly because she is not unlike myself. Or rather, she reminds me much of my past self. She is naive, yes, but it is not from a lack of intelligence. Quite the contrary: it is her romantic heart that wins against her educated mind. <i>“I’</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15007323751722102256" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>"What a horrible thing for her to say—she was crazy then, poor thing?"<br />"Crazy with fear and misery, p’tite. <b>A tropic flower cannot live without sun. A soul cannot live without love.'"</b></i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Miranda, <i>Dragonwyck</i>'s heroine, is a character very near and dear to my heart; mostly because she is not unlike myself. Or rather, she reminds me much of my past self. She is naive, yes, but it is not from a lack of intelligence. Quite the contrary: it is her romantic heart that wins against her educated mind. <i>“I’ve a head stuffed full of silly fancies,”</i> she admits to herself. My head has been up in the clouds of fancies for as long as I can remember. And although Miranda has her fair share of sorrows, she sometimes still manages to keep her childlike wonder and amusement.<br /><br />I turned to <i>Dragonwyck</i> after three very disappointing modern novels in a row. Frustrated, I took up the latest classic I had purchased, <b>begging the Reading Gods that this was the right choice to lift me out of my reading slump. </b><i>Dragonwyck</i> has saved me from the horrors of contemporary literature and marked the beginning of...whatever the opposite of a book slump is called, as I have since raced through <i>three</i> other exceptional novels.<br /><br />There is perhaps not much I can say about <i>Dragonwyck</i> that hasn’t already been said, and even less I can say without giving too much away, but this is just <b>the perfect Gothic with much more. It is a tale of the evils of men, the intuition of women, and the redemption of true love. </b>A literary masterpiece that is full of beautiful prose and characters that are full of life.<br /><br />Today, with our better understanding of human psychology, one could even argue that it’s <b>a story of abuse and mental illness under the guise of passion and romance.</b> (If you are sensitive to these issues, you may want to skip this one. I would be happy to help point out possible triggers, for any book I’ve read, just message me!)<br /><br /><i>Dragonwyck</i> is told in omnipotent third person, which is something I can’t recall reading in a very long time. Rather than chopping up different points of view chapter by chapter,<b> Seton carries us from one character’s mind to the next with great care and elegance. </b>While most of the story comes from our dear Miranda’s eyes, some minor characters, such as the Count, will suddenly jump in for a thought or an anecdote, keeping the perspective fresh and interesting. Though we get to see things from Miranda’s parents’ view, from Jeff, a local doctor, et cetera, <b>we never slip inside Nicholas’s skin: making him all the more mysterious.</b> The book, I imagine, would have been completely different if the reader knew what Nicholas was thinking, and I like that he was left out of this omnipotence. <br /><br />One of the shining moments for me was the visit to Edgar Allen Poe’s cottage. I won’t say anything more, but there are a few other famous American writers that make it into this story, and it was a delight finding these “Easter eggs” sprinkled throughout. <b>They felt like real, breathing, people, not just characters inspired by them.</b><br /><br />Besides these real life figures, I instantly fell in love with Peggy. She is introduced late into the story, but she is so life-like, and her story and situation made me very emotional. My ancestors survived the famine in Ireland just as Peggy did, and I am partially disabled, as she is. <b>Peggy faces horrible discrimination for both being an Irish immigrant and for having a limp, but she is still pure of heart and most importantly, a great friend to Miranda when she needed it most.</b><br /><br />There are bits of history and politics woven into the story as well. There are a few pages commenting on U.S. politics leading up the Civil War that illuminated the subject more than any history book I've read in school. This takes place at a time when many things were changing in the U.S., and while Seton doesn't let any of this overwhelm Miranda's story, she doesn't ignore them, either: a great balancing act that enriches the immersion completely.<br /><br />I would recommend <i>Dragonwyck</i> to anyone who enjoys Gothic literature, or just a very well written, slow burning book. I wish Anya Seton was more recognized, as I feel very late to her train...but<b> I cannot wait to take solace in one of her books again soon.</b><br /><br /><br />___________________________________<br /><br />First thoughts: <br />I absolutely loved this novel. I have nearly two pages of notes and thoughts. I will let my feelings sink in further. Again, my expectations are entirely thrown away, but replaced with something even better. Thank you, Ms. Seton.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15007323751722102256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/775149998" />
    <a title="Dorcas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21426381-dorcas"><img alt="Dorcas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522633335p2/21426381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/775149998?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorcas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorcas" href="/user/show/21426381-dorcas">Dorcas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780395081754" href="/book/show/2365603.Dragonwyck">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21426381-dorcas?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21426381-dorcas?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21426381-dorcas?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21426381-dorcas?shelf=gothic">gothic</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21426381-dorcas?shelf=house-as-character">house-as-character</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer775149998" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer559112513605491510">Dragonwyck is a difficult book to LIKE. And yet its very good. I'm in a quandry...<br/><br/>5 star writing skills<br/>3 star enjoyment<br/>Rounded off to 4 stars<br/><br/>In a nutshell, a country girl has high aspirations and jumps at the chance to leave the farm for an extended visit at her cousin Nicholas' vast estate. (I thought Miranda was much like Hettie from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20563.Adam_Bede' title='Adam Bede by George Eliot' rel='nofollow noopener'>Adam Bede</a> ) Of course, she doesn't know her cousin Nicholas at all; nor does she understand why his corpulent wife, Johanna would rather bury herself in teacakes </span>
  <span id="freeText559112513605491510" style="display:none">Dragonwyck is a difficult book to LIKE. And yet its very good. I'm in a quandry...<br /><br />5 star writing skills<br />3 star enjoyment<br />Rounded off to 4 stars<br /><br />In a nutshell, a country girl has high aspirations and jumps at the chance to leave the farm for an extended visit at her cousin Nicholas' vast estate. (I thought Miranda was much like Hettie from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20563.Adam_Bede" title="Adam Bede by George Eliot" rel="nofollow noopener">Adam Bede</a> ) Of course, she doesn't know her cousin Nicholas at all; nor does she understand why his corpulent wife, Johanna would rather bury herself in teacakes and pastries than cross him. All she sees is his godlike attributes, magnetism and charm. So when Nicholas' wife, Johanna suddenly dies from 'acute gastritis', Miranda slides right into his arms. And wakes up in a nightmare...<br /><br />Its important to understand from the get go that Nicholas is not the hero. He is a sociopath/ egomaniac. ( Think Wolf Larsen, Captain Ahab or even Ted Bundy). So he's not swoonworthy; however, he IS one of the main characters so you see a lot of him. And I was ready to get shed of him much sooner than was the case! But you know, that in itself was skilful writing because the reader could genuinely enter into the heroine's world and feel what she felt.<br /><br />For those of us who have a hard time understanding why someone stays in an abusive relationship instead of 'just leaving ', this book opens our eyes to what manipulation really is. How background plays a part (in both the victim and the abuser), how an abusive person 'recognizes ' their next victim, and how the web is spun so expertly that the victim hardly knows they're caught until theyre stunned powerless to fight...<br /><br />And I suppose its knowing that there's really people like this that takes it out of the realm of what I would term enjoyable "escapism fiction".<br /><br />CONTENT :<br /><br />SEX : None shown to reader explicitly but marital rape is obviously an issue on several occasions.<br /><br />VIOLENCE: domestic violence shown mostly in the form of mental intimidation and physical domination.<br /><br />PROFANITY : Very mild<br /><br />PARANORMAL ELEMENTS : laughing and piano playing is heard by two characters on different occasions when no one else heard it. Whether it was mental illness or ghosts is not clarified.<br /><br />MY RATING : Strong PG or mild PG-13</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1663438255" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1663438255?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mela" href="/user/show/41757430-mela">Mela</a>

        rated it

            Shelves:

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41757430-mela?shelf=american-literature">american-literature</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1663438255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14028237266755569501">it is definitely a very interesting book. According to my experience, it isn't a typical piece, it is hard to mark it as one genre. <br/><br/>First of all, it is in the atmosphere of a gothic story. But it isn't "too much gothic" so someone like me (I mean, someone who isn't a fan of the gothic story) isn't bored. I confess I was even sucked a little in this atmosphere ;-) Anya Seton wrote in the way that I felt like I was been with characters, like I was felt fear with them.<br/><br/><i>"In after years Miranda knew t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText14028237266755569501" style="display:none">it is definitely a very interesting book. According to my experience, it isn't a typical piece, it is hard to mark it as one genre. <br /><br />First of all, it is in the atmosphere of a gothic story. But it isn't "too much gothic" so someone like me (I mean, someone who isn't a fan of the gothic story) isn't bored. I confess I was even sucked a little in this atmosphere ;-) Anya Seton wrote in the way that I felt like I was been with characters, like I was felt fear with them.<br /><br /><i>"In after years Miranda knew that her first sight of Dragonwyck was the most vivid and significant impression of her life. She stared at the fantastic silhouette which loomed dark against the eastern sky, the spires and gables and chimneys dominated in the center by one high tower; and it was as though the good and evil, the happiness and tragedy, which she was to experience under that roof materialized into physical force and struck across the quiet river into her soul"</i><br /><br />Secondly, it is a great historical fiction. Seton made the past nearer. She described the world in the way that I can almost feel that I saw it on my own eyes. And most of all, I can understand characters not according to my modern views and opinions but according to their views and belief. Like in her <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33609.Katherine" title="Katherine by Anya Seton" rel="nofollow noopener">Katherine</a> it is the strongest party book.<br /><br />And last but not least, persons in this story are human. They aren't black or white. There isn't a villain like in a some Hollywod movie. Like in the real life, everybody is good and bad. Everybody has some dark sides. But everyone deals with it in different way, because everyone is different (you can call it genes, soul - as you like) and has different life/experiences. So, one person becomes better person and other not. But we all are just human and at the end we all are the same...<br /><br />It is really a good book. I will be remembered it long. Especially, when I will see or read about <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[oleander <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> or anti-rent war or steamboat races I will always recall this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14028237266755569501" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_82285238" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/82285238" />
    <a title="Laura" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17116-laura"><img alt="Laura" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1399226743p2/17116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/82285238?book_show_action=true">Dec 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/17116-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17116-laura?shelf=borrowed-from-public-library">borrowed-from-public-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer82285238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10607313944684189752">Normally I'm annoyed when an author throws real people into a historical novel, but I thought Anya Seton did it rather well. I never felt like I was being beaten over the head with how familiar she was with the authors in the book (Poe, Melville, etc), or that Miranda was lost behind all the other characters. I actually enjoyed the book so much that I'll probably end up buying it to read again, even though I haven't re-read a book in about four years (something you can do when you have a great l</span>
  <span id="freeText10607313944684189752" style="display:none">Normally I'm annoyed when an author throws real people into a historical novel, but I thought Anya Seton did it rather well. I never felt like I was being beaten over the head with how familiar she was with the authors in the book (Poe, Melville, etc), or that Miranda was lost behind all the other characters. I actually enjoyed the book so much that I'll probably end up buying it to read again, even though I haven't re-read a book in about four years (something you can do when you have a great library). I do wish I hadn't read Philippa Gregory's afterword, because I sort of noticed the flaws she points out while reading the book, but I wasn't that aware of them. Once she mentioned them, I was a little crestfallen because they were stuck in my head. The worst flaw to me was the romance part, because I saw absolutely no reason that the two should be in love with each other. Anyway, I really loved the book.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2759795133" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2759795133" />
    <a title="Sarah Baker" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5309165-sarah-baker"><img alt="Sarah Baker" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603231043p2/5309165.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2759795133?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Baker" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Baker" href="/user/show/5309165-sarah-baker">Sarah Baker</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19068754-dragonwyck">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5309165-sarah-baker?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2759795133" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2471902994843805872">Genre: Historical Fiction<br/>Suggested Age: Adult (trigger warnings for spousal abuse)<br/>What is this Book About?: It's 1844, and Miranda Wells is 18 and ready to see the world. The life of a farm-girl holds no appeal for her. So when a letter comes from a mysterious cousin (incidentally, no relation by blood) inviting her to come and live at his estate, Dragonwyck, and to occasionally serve as a teacher to his six-year old daughter, it seems like a dream come true. And meeting Nicholas Van Ryn, she is</span>
  <span id="freeText2471902994843805872" style="display:none">Genre: Historical Fiction<br />Suggested Age: Adult (trigger warnings for spousal abuse)<br />What is this Book About?: It's 1844, and Miranda Wells is 18 and ready to see the world. The life of a farm-girl holds no appeal for her. So when a letter comes from a mysterious cousin (incidentally, no relation by blood) inviting her to come and live at his estate, Dragonwyck, and to occasionally serve as a teacher to his six-year old daughter, it seems like a dream come true. And meeting Nicholas Van Ryn, she is swept off of her feet. He's charming and debonair, but he is subject to black moods. He sees potential in Miranda to turn her from a country bumpkin into a lady. And very slowly, Miranda begins to fall in love. But Nicholas is married. He hates his wife, and encourages Miranda's infatuation. When Johanna Van Ryn dies after a short illness, Miranda becomes the next Mrs. Van Ryn. But Nicholas is a different man after their marriage. His mood swings and temperament worsen, leaving Miranda to wonder if she will meet an untimely end as well.<br />My Review: I enjoyed this - Gothic romance without the infuriatingly dense language of the 19th century. Miranda is both sympathetic and occasionally unlikable, most of which stems from her "coarse" upbringing and naivety of what "proper" society expects. The first half of this book is genteel and borderline soppy, but it does acknowledge the dark. I included a trigger warning on this one, which I don't usually do. However, the abusive situation came out of left field and, while not explicit, it was enough to seriously rattle me (likely because the rest is genteel). After their wedding, the tone becomes darker. The manipulation and callousness that both Miranda and Nicholas display is disheartening. But Miranda improves greatly, maturing into a kind and thoughtful woman. And the ending...well it gives a sweeter resolution than the lead up would suggest.<br />(If you can track down the 1946 movie version [alas, not in our system, streaming, or even readily available on DVD, but there are clips up on YouTube], do yourself a favor and watch it. Gene Tierney and Vincent Price play off of each other so well! And the movie glosses past most of the worst darkness and nastiness with a vastly different end.)<br />Three Words That Describe This Book: Gothic, Dramatic, Surprising<br />Give this a try if you like…Gone With The Wind, Edgar Allen Poe, Crimson Peak<br />Rating: (out of 5)​​ 4/5</span>
  <a data-text-id="2471902994843805872" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gVNzfqdl6jz11FSLYFWQZngIasoXZmBZOlgF2oQd5JiO0u4UhjSm6e0VVNciIYBgdiN6+glBRLh525sLFhklFw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('rzuQs9QvT8TzPLQ99aXbngv8IPHE6F6janceQ7IyQDWgug3Z9X4DEev9tGG30cuYBdcwwdrPekIp9ICSIDaBug==')})
  }

Present day, London: When Sophie discovers a photograph of her great aunt Vivi from World War Two, it throws her into a world of confusion. Because, as she learns about this secret relative, she quickly realises that the photograph doesn’t fit with her family’s story. It shows Vivi leaving an address associated with a spy network in London – a place she had no reason to be – and it is dated right before she disappeared.  Meanwhile Sophie’s own life feels as blasted and bombed as the Blitzed city in the photograph she’s looking at. Her beautiful daughter – as full of joy and wild energy as Vivi had apparently once been – is gone; and Sophie’s heart has been left broken into pieces.  Retreating to the family home in rural Cornwall to seek solace from her pain and the feelings of guilt that she could have done more to protect her daughter, Sophie finds herself becoming obsessed with Vivi’s life.  But nothing can prepare Sophie for what she is about to uncover – the story of a woman who risked everything for the person she loved the most; and a secret family history that could be the key to Sophie’s own future.  A powerful, haunting and unforgettable read about love, heartbreak and betrayal set in Second World War Britain and France.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18930.Anya_Seton">About Anya Seton</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/18930.Anya_Seton"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1224813438p3/18930.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/18930.Anya_Seton">Anya Seton
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
687
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4858260244914623557">Anya Seton (January 23, 1904 (although the year is often misstated to be 1906 or 1916) - November 8, 1990) was the pen name of the American author of historical romances, Ann Seton.<br/><br/>Ann Seton was born in New York, New York, and died in Old Greenwich, Connecticut. She was the daughter of English-born naturalist and pioneer of the Boy Scouts of America, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/31707.Ernest_Thompson_Seton' title='Ernest Thompson Seton' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ernest Thompson Seton</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3916395.Grace_Gallatin_Seton_Thompson' title='Grace Gallatin Seton-Thompson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Grace Gallatin Seton-</a></span>
  <span id="freeText4858260244914623557" style="display:none">Anya Seton (January 23, 1904 (although the year is often misstated to be 1906 or 1916) - November 8, 1990) was the pen name of the American author of historical romances, Ann Seton.<br /><br />Ann Seton was born in New York, New York, and died in Old Greenwich, Connecticut. She was the daughter of English-born naturalist and pioneer of the Boy Scouts of America, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/31707.Ernest_Thompson_Seton" title="Ernest Thompson Seton" rel="nofollow noopener">Ernest Thompson Seton</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3916395.Grace_Gallatin_Seton_Thompson" title="Grace Gallatin Seton-Thompson" rel="nofollow noopener">Grace Gallatin Seton-Thompson</a>. She is interred at Putnam Cemetery in Greenwich.<br /><br />Her historical novels were noted for how extensively she researched the historical facts, and some of them were best-sellers.[citation needed] Dragonwyck (1941) and Foxfire (1950) were both made into Hollywood films. Two of her books are classics in their genre and continue in their popularity to the present; Katherine, the story of Katherine Swynford, the mistress and eventual wife of John of Gaunt, and their children, who eventually became the basis for the Tudor and Stuart families of England, and Green Darkness, the story of a modern couple plagued by their past life incarnations. Most of her novels have been recently republished, several with forewords by Philippa Gregory.<br /><br />Her novel Devil Water concerns James, the luckless Earl of Derwentwater and his involvement with the Jacobite rising of 1715. She also narrates the story of his brother Charles, beheaded after the 1745 rebellion, the last man to die for the cause. The action of the novel moves back and forth between Northumberland, Tyneside, London and America.<br /><br />Anya Seton stated that the book developed out of her love for Northumberland. Anya certainly visited her Snowdon cousins at Felton. Billy Pigg, the celebrated Northumbrian piper played 'Derwentwater's Farewell' especially for her. The novel shows her typical thorough research of events and places, though the accents are a little wayward. Anya Seton said that her greatest debt of all was to Miss Amy Flagg of Westoe Village in South Shields, her father's birthplace.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4858260244914623557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
